2277         /** Package-private version of lookup which is trusted. */
2278         static final Lookup IMPL_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, TRUSTED);
2279 
2280         /** Version of lookup which is trusted minimally.
2281          *  It can only be used to create method handles to publicly accessible
2282          *  members in packages that are exported unconditionally.
2283          */
2284         static final Lookup PUBLIC_LOOKUP = new Lookup(Object.class, null, UNCONDITIONAL);
2285 
2286         static final JavaLangAccess JLA = SharedSecrets.getJavaLangAccess();
2287 
2288         private static void checkUnprivilegedlookupClass(Class<?> lookupClass) {
2289             String name = lookupClass.getName();
2290             if (name.startsWith("java.lang.invoke."))
2291                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal lookupClass: "+lookupClass);
2292         }
2293 
2294         /**
2295          * Displays the name of the class from which lookups are to be made,
2296          * followed by "/" and the name of the {@linkplain #previousLookupClass()
2297          * previous lookup class} if present.
2298          * (The name is the one reported by {@link java.lang.Class#getName() Class.getName}.)
2299          * If there are restrictions on the access permitted to this lookup,
2300          * this is indicated by adding a suffix to the class name, consisting
2301          * of a slash and a keyword.  The keyword represents the strongest
2302          * allowed access, and is chosen as follows:
2303          * <ul>
2304          * <li>If no access is allowed, the suffix is "/noaccess".
2305          * <li>If only unconditional access is allowed, the suffix is "/publicLookup".
2306          * <li>If only public access to types in exported packages is allowed, the suffix is "/public".
2307          * <li>If only public and module access are allowed, the suffix is "/module".
2308          * <li>If public and package access are allowed, the suffix is "/package".
2309          * <li>If public, package, and private access are allowed, the suffix is "/private".
2310          * </ul>
2311          * If none of the above cases apply, it is the case that full access
2312          * (public, module, package, private, and protected) is allowed.
2313          * In this case, no suffix is added.
2314          * This is true only of an object obtained originally from
2315          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#lookup MethodHandles.lookup}.
2316          * Objects created by {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.Lookup#in Lookup.in}
2317          * always have restricted access, and will display a suffix.
2318          * <p>
2319          * (It may seem strange that protected access should be
2320          * stronger than private access.  Viewed independently from
2321          * package access, protected access is the first to be lost,
2322          * because it requires a direct subclass relationship between
2323          * caller and callee.)
2324          * @see #in
2325          *
2326          * @revised 9
2327          * @spec JPMS
2328          */
2329         @Override
2330         public String toString() {
2331             String cname = lookupClass.getName();
2332             if (prevLookupClass != null)
2333                 cname += "/" + prevLookupClass.getName();
2334             switch (allowedModes) {
2335             case 0:  // no privileges
2336                 return cname + "/noaccess";
2337             case UNCONDITIONAL:
2338                 return cname + "/publicLookup";
2339             case PUBLIC:
2340                 return cname + "/public";
2341             case PUBLIC|MODULE:
2342                 return cname + "/module";
2343             case PUBLIC|PACKAGE:
2344             case PUBLIC|MODULE|PACKAGE:
2345                 return cname + "/package";
2346             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~PROTECTED):
2347             case FULL_POWER_MODES & ~(PROTECTED|MODULE):
2348                 return cname + "/private";
2349             case FULL_POWER_MODES:
2350             case FULL_POWER_MODES & (~MODULE):
2351                 return cname;
2352             case TRUSTED:
2353                 return "/trusted";  // internal only; not exported
2354             default:  // Should not happen, but it's a bitfield...
2355                 cname = cname + "/" + Integer.toHexString(allowedModes);
2356                 assert(false) : cname;
2357                 return cname;
2358             }
2359         }
2360 
2361         /**
2362          * Produces a method handle for a static method.
2363          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method.
2364          * (Since static methods do not take receivers, there is no
2365          * additional receiver argument inserted into the method handle type,
2366          * as there would be with {@link #findVirtual findVirtual} or {@link #findSpecial findSpecial}.)
2367          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2368          * <p>
2369          * The returned method handle will have
2370          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2371          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2372          * <p>
2373          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
2374          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2375          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2376          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2377 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2378 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2379 ...
2380 MethodHandle MH_asList = publicLookup().findStatic(Arrays.class,
2381   "asList", methodType(List.class, Object[].class));
2382 assertEquals("[x, y]", MH_asList.invoke("x", "y").toString());
2383          * }</pre></blockquote>
2384          * @param refc the class from which the method is accessed
2385          * @param name the name of the method
2386          * @param type the type of the method
2387          * @return the desired method handle
2388          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2389          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2390          *                                or if the method is not {@code static},
2391          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2392          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2393          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2394          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2395          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2396          */
2397         public MethodHandle findStatic(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2398             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeStatic, refc, name, type);
2399             // resolveOrFail could return a non-static <init> method if present
2400             // detect and throw NSME before producing a MethodHandle
2401             if (!method.isStatic() && name.equals("<init>")) {
2402                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
2403             }
2404 
2405             return getDirectMethod(REF_invokeStatic, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2406         }
2407 
2408         /**
2409          * Produces a method handle for a virtual method.
2410          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2411          * with the receiver type (usually {@code refc}) prepended.
2412          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2413          * <p>
2414          * When called, the handle will treat the first argument as a receiver
2415          * and, for non-private methods, dispatch on the receiver's type to determine which method
2416          * implementation to enter.
2417          * For private methods the named method in {@code refc} will be invoked on the receiver.
2418          * (The dispatching action is identical with that performed by an
2419          * {@code invokevirtual} or {@code invokeinterface} instruction.)
2420          * <p>
2421          * The first argument will be of type {@code refc} if the lookup
2422          * class has full privileges to access the member.  Otherwise
2423          * the member must be {@code protected} and the first argument
2424          * will be restricted in type to the lookup class.
2425          * <p>
2426          * The returned method handle will have
2427          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2428          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2429          * <p>
2430          * Because of the general <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">equivalence</a> between {@code invokevirtual}
2431          * instructions and method handles produced by {@code findVirtual},
2432          * if the class is {@code MethodHandle} and the name string is
2433          * {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke}, the resulting
2434          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2435          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#exactInvoker MethodHandles.exactInvoker} or
2436          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#invoker MethodHandles.invoker}
2437          * with the same {@code type} argument.
2438          * <p>
2439          * If the class is {@code VarHandle} and the name string corresponds to
2440          * the name of a signature-polymorphic access mode method, the resulting
2441          * method handle is equivalent to one produced by
2442          * {@link java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles#varHandleInvoker} with
2443          * the access mode corresponding to the name string and with the same
2444          * {@code type} arguments.
2445          * <p>
2446          * <b>Example:</b>
2447          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2448 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2449 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2450 ...
2451 MethodHandle MH_concat = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2452   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
2453 MethodHandle MH_hashCode = publicLookup().findVirtual(Object.class,
2454   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2455 MethodHandle MH_hashCode_String = publicLookup().findVirtual(String.class,
2456   "hashCode", methodType(int.class));
2457 assertEquals("xy", (String) MH_concat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
2458 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode.invokeExact((Object)"xy"));
2459 assertEquals("xy".hashCode(), (int) MH_hashCode_String.invokeExact("xy"));
2460 // interface method:
2461 MethodHandle MH_subSequence = publicLookup().findVirtual(CharSequence.class,
2462   "subSequence", methodType(CharSequence.class, int.class, int.class));
2463 assertEquals("def", MH_subSequence.invoke("abcdefghi", 3, 6).toString());
2464 // constructor "internal method" must be accessed differently:
2465 MethodType MT_newString = methodType(void.class); //()V for new String()
2466 try { assertEquals("impossible", lookup()
2467         .findVirtual(String.class, "<init>", MT_newString));
2468  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2469 MethodHandle MH_newString = publicLookup()
2470   .findConstructor(String.class, MT_newString);
2471 assertEquals("", (String) MH_newString.invokeExact());
2472          * }</pre></blockquote>
2473          *
2474          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2475          * @param name the name of the method
2476          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2477          * @return the desired method handle
2478          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2479          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2480          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2481          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2482          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2483          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2484          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2485          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2486          */
2487         public MethodHandle findVirtual(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2488             if (refc == MethodHandle.class) {
2489                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForMH(name, type);
2490                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2491             } else if (refc == VarHandle.class) {
2492                 MethodHandle mh = findVirtualForVH(name, type);
2493                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
2494             }
2495             byte refKind = (refc.isInterface() ? REF_invokeInterface : REF_invokeVirtual);
2496             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(refKind, refc, name, type);
2497             return getDirectMethod(refKind, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2498         }
2499         private MethodHandle findVirtualForMH(String name, MethodType type) {
2500             // these names require special lookups because of the implicit MethodType argument
2501             if ("invoke".equals(name))
2502                 return invoker(type);
2503             if ("invokeExact".equals(name))
2504                 return exactInvoker(type);
2505             assert(!MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(name));
2506             return null;
2507         }
2508         private MethodHandle findVirtualForVH(String name, MethodType type) {
2509             try {
2510                 return varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode.valueFromMethodName(name), type);
2511             } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
2512                 return null;
2513             }
2514         }
2515 
2516         /**
2517          * Produces a method handle which creates an object and initializes it, using
2518          * the constructor of the specified type.
2519          * The parameter types of the method handle will be those of the constructor,
2520          * while the return type will be a reference to the constructor's class.
2521          * The constructor and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
2522          * <p>
2523          * The requested type must have a return type of {@code void}.
2524          * (This is consistent with the JVM's treatment of constructor type descriptors.)
2525          * <p>
2526          * The returned method handle will have
2527          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2528          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2529          * <p>
2530          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
2531          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2532          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2533          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2534 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2535 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2536 ...
2537 MethodHandle MH_newArrayList = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2538   ArrayList.class, methodType(void.class, Collection.class));
2539 Collection orig = Arrays.asList("x", "y");
2540 Collection copy = (ArrayList) MH_newArrayList.invokeExact(orig);
2541 assert(orig != copy);
2542 assertEquals(orig, copy);
2543 // a variable-arity constructor:
2544 MethodHandle MH_newProcessBuilder = publicLookup().findConstructor(
2545   ProcessBuilder.class, methodType(void.class, String[].class));
2546 ProcessBuilder pb = (ProcessBuilder)
2547   MH_newProcessBuilder.invoke("x", "y", "z");
2548 assertEquals("[x, y, z]", pb.command().toString());
2549          * }</pre></blockquote>
2550          *
2551          * @apiNote
2552          * This method does not find a static {@code <init>} factory method as it is invoked
2553          * via {@code invokestatic} bytecode as opposed to {@code invokespecial} for an
2554          * object constructor.  To look up static {@code <init>} factory method, use
2555          * the {@link #findStatic(Class, String, MethodType) findStatic} method.
2556          *
2557          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2558          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted, and a void return type
2559          * @return the desired method handle
2560          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the constructor does not exist
2561          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
2562          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2563          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2564          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2565          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2566          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2567          */
2568         public MethodHandle findConstructor(Class<?> refc, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2569             if (refc.isArray()) {
2570                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("no constructor for array class: " + refc.getName());
2571             }
2572             if (type.returnType() != void.class) {
2573                 throw new NoSuchMethodException("Constructors must have void return type: " + refc.getName());
2574             }
2575             String name = "<init>";
2576             MemberName ctor = resolveOrFail(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2577             return getDirectConstructor(refc, ctor);
2578         }
2579 
2580         /**
2581          * Looks up a class by name from the lookup context defined by this {@code Lookup} object,
2582          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if resolved</a> by an {@code ldc} instruction.
2583          * Such a resolution, as specified in JVMS 5.4.3.1 section, attempts to locate and load the class,
2584          * and then determines whether the class is accessible to this lookup object.
2585          * <p>
2586          * The lookup context here is determined by the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class},
2587          * its class loader, and the {@linkplain #lookupModes() lookup modes}.
2588          *
2589          * @param targetName the fully qualified name of the class to be looked up.
2590          * @return the requested class.
2591          * @throws SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2592          *                           <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2593          * @throws LinkageError if the linkage fails
2594          * @throws ClassNotFoundException if the class cannot be loaded by the lookup class' loader.
2595          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible, using the allowed access
2596          * modes.
2597          * @since 9
2598          * @jvms 5.4.3.1 Class and Interface Resolution
2599          */
2600         public Class<?> findClass(String targetName) throws ClassNotFoundException, IllegalAccessException {
2601             Class<?> targetClass = Class.forName(targetName, false, lookupClass.getClassLoader());
2602             return accessClass(targetClass);
2603         }
2604 
2605         /**
2606          * Determines if a class can be accessed from the lookup context defined by
2607          * this {@code Lookup} object. The static initializer of the class is not run.
2608          * <p>
2609          * If the {@code targetClass} is in the same module as the lookup class,
2610          * the lookup class is {@code LC} in module {@code M1} and
2611          * the previous lookup class is in module {@code M0} or
2612          * {@code null} if not present,
2613          * {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if one of the following is true:
2614          * <ul>
2615          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PRIVATE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2616          *     {@code LC} or other class in the same nest of {@code LC}.</li>
2617          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PACKAGE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2618          *     in the same runtime package of {@code LC}.</li>
2619          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #MODULE} access, {@code targetClass} is
2620          *     a public type in {@code M1}.</li>
2621          * <li>If this lookup has {@link #PUBLIC} access, {@code targetClass} is
2622          *     a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} to at least  {@code M0}
2623          *     if the previous lookup class is present; otherwise, {@code targetClass}
2624          *     is a public type in a package exported by {@code M1} unconditionally.</li>
2625          * </ul>
2626          *
2627          * <p>
2628          * Otherwise, if this lookup has {@link #UNCONDITIONAL} access, this lookup
2629          * can access public types in all modules when the type is in a package
2630          * that is exported unconditionally.
2631          * <p>
2632          * Otherwise, the target class is in a different module from {@code lookupClass},
2633          * and if this lookup does not have {@code PUBLIC} access, {@code lookupClass}
2634          * is inaccessible.
2635          * <p>
2636          * Otherwise, if this lookup has no {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2637          * {@code M1} is the module containing {@code lookupClass} and
2638          * {@code M2} is the module containing {@code targetClass},
2639          * then {@code targetClass} is accessible if and only if
2640          * <ul>
2641          * <li>{@code M1} reads {@code M2}, and
2642          * <li>{@code targetClass} is public and in a package exported by
2643          *     {@code M2} at least to {@code M1}.
2644          * </ul>
2645          * <p>
2646          * Otherwise, if this lookup has a {@linkplain #previousLookupClass() previous lookup class},
2647          * {@code M1} and {@code M2} are as before, and {@code M0} is the module
2648          * containing the previous lookup class, then {@code targetClass} is accessible
2649          * if and only if one of the following is true:
2650          * <ul>
2651          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M0} and {@code M1}
2652          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M0} and the type is
2653          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M1}.
2654          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in {@code M1} and {@code M0}
2655          *     {@linkplain Module#reads reads} {@code M1} and the type is
2656          *     in a package that is exported to at least {@code M0}.
2657          * <li>{@code targetClass} is in a third module {@code M2} and both {@code M0}
2658          *     and {@code M1} reads {@code M2} and the type is in a package
2659          *     that is exported to at least both {@code M0} and {@code M2}.
2660          * </ul>
2661          * <p>
2662          * Otherwise, {@code targetClass} is not accessible.
2663          *
2664          * @param targetClass the class to be access-checked
2665          * @return the class that has been access-checked
2666          * @throws IllegalAccessException if the class is not accessible from the lookup class
2667          * and previous lookup class, if present, using the allowed access modes.
2668          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2669          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2670          * @since 9
2671          * @see <a href="#cross-module-lookup">Cross-module lookups</a>
2672          */
2673         public Class<?> accessClass(Class<?> targetClass) throws IllegalAccessException {
2674             if (!VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(targetClass, lookupClass, prevLookupClass, allowedModes)) {
2675                 throw new MemberName(targetClass).makeAccessException("access violation", this);
2676             }
2677             checkSecurityManager(targetClass, null);
2678             return targetClass;
2679         }
2680 
2681         /**
2682          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a virtual method.
2683          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
2684          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
2685          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
2686          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
2687          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
2688          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
2689          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible
2690          * to the lookup object.
2691          * <p>
2692          * Before method resolution,
2693          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
2694          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
2695          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
2696          * privileges, the access fails.
2697          * <p>
2698          * The returned method handle will have
2699          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
2700          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
2701          * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
2702          * <em>(Note:  JVM internal methods named {@code "<init>"} are not visible to this API,
2703          * even though the {@code invokespecial} instruction can refer to them
2704          * in special circumstances.  Use {@link #findConstructor findConstructor}
2705          * to access instance initialization methods in a safe manner.)</em>
2706          * <p><b>Example:</b>
2707          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
2708 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
2709 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
2710 ...
2711 static class Listie extends ArrayList {
2712   public String toString() { return "[wee Listie]"; }
2713   static Lookup lookup() { return MethodHandles.lookup(); }
2714 }
2715 ...
2716 // no access to constructor via invokeSpecial:
2717 MethodHandle MH_newListie = Listie.lookup()
2718   .findConstructor(Listie.class, methodType(void.class));
2719 Listie l = (Listie) MH_newListie.invokeExact();
2720 try { assertEquals("impossible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2721         Listie.class, "<init>", methodType(void.class), Listie.class));
2722  } catch (NoSuchMethodException ex) { } // OK
2723 // access to super and self methods via invokeSpecial:
2724 MethodHandle MH_super = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2725   ArrayList.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2726 MethodHandle MH_this = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2727   Listie.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2728 MethodHandle MH_duper = Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2729   Object.class, "toString" , methodType(String.class), Listie.class);
2730 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_super.invokeExact(l));
2731 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(l));
2732 assertEquals("[]", (String) MH_duper.invokeExact(l)); // ArrayList method
2733 try { assertEquals("inaccessible", Listie.lookup().findSpecial(
2734         String.class, "toString", methodType(String.class), Listie.class));
2735  } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) { } // OK
2736 Listie subl = new Listie() { public String toString() { return "[subclass]"; } };
2737 assertEquals(""+l, (String) MH_this.invokeExact(subl)); // Listie method
2738          * }</pre></blockquote>
2739          *
2740          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2741          * @param name the name of the method (which must not be "&lt;init&gt;")
2742          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
2743          * @param specialCaller the proposed calling class to perform the {@code invokespecial}
2744          * @return the desired method handle
2745          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
2746          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
2747          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
2748          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
2749          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
2750          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2751          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2752          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2753          */
2754         public MethodHandle findSpecial(Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type,
2755                                         Class<?> specialCaller) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
2756             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, refc);
2757             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
2758             MemberName method = specialLookup.resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
2759             return specialLookup.getDirectMethod(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
2760         }
2761 
2762         /**
2763          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a non-static field.
2764          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2765          * value type.
2766          * The method handle's single argument will be the instance containing
2767          * the field.
2768          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2769          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2770          * @param name the field's name
2771          * @param type the field's type
2772          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2773          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2774          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2775          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2776          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2777          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2778          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2779          */
2780         public MethodHandle findGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2781             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, refc, name, type);
2782             return getDirectField(REF_getField, refc, field);
2783         }
2784 
2785         /**
2786          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a non-static field.
2787          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2788          * The method handle will take two arguments, the instance containing
2789          * the field, and the value to be stored.
2790          * The second argument will be of the field's value type.
2791          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2792          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2793          * @param name the field's name
2794          * @param type the field's type
2795          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2796          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2797          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2798          *                                or {@code final}
2799          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2800          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2801          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2802          * @see #findVarHandle(Class, String, Class)
2803          */
2804         public MethodHandle findSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2805             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, refc, name, type);
2806             return getDirectField(REF_putField, refc, field);
2807         }
2808 
2809         /**
2810          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a non-static field {@code name}
2811          * of type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code recv}.
2812          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has one
2813          * coordinate type, {@code recv}.
2814          * <p>
2815          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2816          * class.
2817          * <p>
2818          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2819          * the following conditions:
2820          * <ul>
2821          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2822          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2823          *     modes are unsupported.
2824          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2825          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2826          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
2827          *     access modes are unsupported.
2828          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2829          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2830          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2831          *     unsupported.
2832          * </ul>
2833          * <p>
2834          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2835          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2836          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2837          * access modes.
2838          * <p>
2839          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2840          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2841          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2842          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2843          * @apiNote
2844          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2845          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2846          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2847          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2848          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2849          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2850          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2851          * unexpectedly fail.
2852          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2853          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2854          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2855          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2856          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2857          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2858          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2859          * details).
2860          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2861          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2862          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2863          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2864          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2865          * @param recv the receiver class, of type {@code R}, that declares the
2866          * non-static field
2867          * @param name the field's name
2868          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2869          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields.
2870          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2871          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is {@code static}
2872          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2873          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2874          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2875          * @since 9
2876          */
2877         public VarHandle findVarHandle(Class<?> recv, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2878             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getField, recv, name, type);
2879             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putField, recv, name, type);
2880             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getField, REF_putField, recv, getField, putField);
2881         }
2882 
2883         /**
2884          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a static field.
2885          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
2886          * value type.
2887          * The method handle will take no arguments.
2888          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2889          * <p>
2890          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2891          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2892          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2893          * @param name the field's name
2894          * @param type the field's type
2895          * @return a method handle which can load values from the field
2896          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2897          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2898          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2899          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2900          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2901          */
2902         public MethodHandle findStaticGetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2903             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, refc, name, type);
2904             return getDirectField(REF_getStatic, refc, field);
2905         }
2906 
2907         /**
2908          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a static field.
2909          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
2910          * The method handle will take a single
2911          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
2912          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
2913          * <p>
2914          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
2915          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2916          * @param refc the class or interface from which the method is accessed
2917          * @param name the field's name
2918          * @param type the field's type
2919          * @return a method handle which can store values into the field
2920          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2921          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2922          *                                or is {@code final}
2923          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2924          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2925          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
2926          */
2927         public MethodHandle findStaticSetter(Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
2928             MemberName field = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, refc, name, type);
2929             return getDirectField(REF_putStatic, refc, field);
2930         }
2931 
2932         /**
2933          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a static field {@code name} of
2934          * type {@code type} declared in a class of type {@code decl}.
2935          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code type} and it has no
2936          * coordinate types.
2937          * <p>
2938          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
2939          * class.
2940          * <p>
2941          * If the returned VarHandle is operated on, the declaring class will be
2942          * initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
2943          * <p>
2944          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
2945          * the following conditions:
2946          * <ul>
2947          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
2948          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
2949          *     modes are unsupported.
2950          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
2951          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
2952          *     {@code float}, or {@code double}, then numeric atomic update
2953          *     access modes are unsupported.
2954          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
2955          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
2956          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
2957          *     unsupported.
2958          * </ul>
2959          * <p>
2960          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
2961          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
2962          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
2963          * access modes.
2964          * <p>
2965          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
2966          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
2967          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
2968          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
2969          * @apiNote
2970          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
2971          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
2972          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
2973          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
2974          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
2975          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
2976          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
2977          * unexpectedly fail.
2978          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
2979          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
2980          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
2981          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
2982          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
2983          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
2984          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
2985          * details).
2986          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
2987          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
2988          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
2989          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
2990          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
2991          * @param decl the class that declares the static field
2992          * @param name the field's name
2993          * @param type the field's type, of type {@code T}
2994          * @return a VarHandle giving access to a static field
2995          * @throws NoSuchFieldException if the field does not exist
2996          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails, or if the field is not {@code static}
2997          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
2998          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
2999          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3000          * @since 9
3001          */
3002         public VarHandle findStaticVarHandle(Class<?> decl, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3003             MemberName getField = resolveOrFail(REF_getStatic, decl, name, type);
3004             MemberName putField = resolveOrFail(REF_putStatic, decl, name, type);
3005             return getFieldVarHandle(REF_getStatic, REF_putStatic, decl, getField, putField);
3006         }
3007 
3008         /**
3009          * Produces an early-bound method handle for a non-static method.
3010          * The receiver must have a supertype {@code defc} in which a method
3011          * of the given name and type is accessible to the lookup class.
3012          * The method and all its argument types must be accessible to the lookup object.
3013          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3014          * without any insertion of an additional receiver parameter.
3015          * The given receiver will be bound into the method handle,
3016          * so that every call to the method handle will invoke the
3017          * requested method on the given receiver.
3018          * <p>
3019          * The returned method handle will have
3020          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3021          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set
3022          * <em>and</em> the trailing array argument is not the only argument.
3023          * (If the trailing array argument is the only argument,
3024          * the given receiver value will be bound to it.)
3025          * <p>
3026          * This is almost equivalent to the following code, with some differences noted below:
3027          * <blockquote><pre>{@code
3028 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
3029 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
3030 ...
3031 MethodHandle mh0 = lookup().findVirtual(defc, name, type);
3032 MethodHandle mh1 = mh0.bindTo(receiver);
3033 mh1 = mh1.withVarargs(mh0.isVarargsCollector());
3034 return mh1;
3035          * }</pre></blockquote>
3036          * where {@code defc} is either {@code receiver.getClass()} or a super
3037          * type of that class, in which the requested method is accessible
3038          * to the lookup class.
3039          * (Unlike {@code bind}, {@code bindTo} does not preserve variable arity.
3040          * Also, {@code bindTo} may throw a {@code ClassCastException} in instances where {@code bind} would
3041          * throw an {@code IllegalAccessException}, as in the case where the member is {@code protected} and
3042          * the receiver is restricted by {@code findVirtual} to the lookup class.)
3043          * @param receiver the object from which the method is accessed
3044          * @param name the name of the method
3045          * @param type the type of the method, with the receiver argument omitted
3046          * @return the desired method handle
3047          * @throws NoSuchMethodException if the method does not exist
3048          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3049          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3050          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3051          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3052          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3053          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3054          * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
3055          * @see #findVirtual
3056          */
3057         public MethodHandle bind(Object receiver, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3058             Class<? extends Object> refc = receiver.getClass(); // may get NPE
3059             MemberName method = resolveOrFail(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, name, type);
3060             MethodHandle mh = getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(refc, method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3061             if (!mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().isAssignableFrom(receiver.getClass())) {
3062                 throw new IllegalAccessException("The restricted defining class " +
3063                                                  mh.type().leadingReferenceParameter().getName() +
3064                                                  " is not assignable from receiver class " +
3065                                                  receiver.getClass().getName());
3066             }
3067             return mh.bindArgumentL(0, receiver).setVarargs(method);
3068         }
3069 
3070         /**
3071          * Makes a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3072          * to <i>m</i>, if the lookup class has permission.
3073          * If <i>m</i> is non-static, the receiver argument is treated as an initial argument.
3074          * If <i>m</i> is virtual, overriding is respected on every call.
3075          * Unlike the Core Reflection API, exceptions are <em>not</em> wrapped.
3076          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3077          * with the receiver type prepended (but only if it is non-static).
3078          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3079          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3080          * If <i>m</i> is not public, do not share the resulting handle with untrusted parties.
3081          * <p>
3082          * The returned method handle will have
3083          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3084          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3085          * <p>
3086          * If <i>m</i> is static, and
3087          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the method's class will
3088          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3089          * @param m the reflected method
3090          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3091          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3092          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3093          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3094          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3095          */
3096         public MethodHandle unreflect(Method m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3097             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == MethodHandle.class) {
3098                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForMH(m);
3099                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3100             }
3101             if (m.getDeclaringClass() == VarHandle.class) {
3102                 MethodHandle mh = unreflectForVH(m);
3103                 if (mh != null)  return mh;
3104             }
3105             MemberName method = new MemberName(m);
3106             byte refKind = method.getReferenceKind();
3107             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial)
3108                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3109             assert(method.isMethod());
3110             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3111             Lookup lookup = m.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3112             return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3113         }
3114         private MethodHandle unreflectForMH(Method m) {
3115             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3116             if (MemberName.isMethodHandleInvokeName(m.getName()))
3117                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeMethodHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3118             return null;
3119         }
3120         private MethodHandle unreflectForVH(Method m) {
3121             // these names require special lookups because they throw UnsupportedOperationException
3122             if (MemberName.isVarHandleMethodInvokeName(m.getName()))
3123                 return MethodHandleImpl.fakeVarHandleInvoke(new MemberName(m));
3124             return null;
3125         }
3126 
3127         /**
3128          * Produces a method handle for a reflected method.
3129          * It will bypass checks for overriding methods on the receiver,
3130          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#equiv">as if called</a> from an {@code invokespecial}
3131          * instruction from within the explicitly specified {@code specialCaller}.
3132          * The type of the method handle will be that of the method,
3133          * with a suitably restricted receiver type prepended.
3134          * (The receiver type will be {@code specialCaller} or a subtype.)
3135          * If the method's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3136          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class,
3137          * as if {@code invokespecial} instruction were being linked.
3138          * <p>
3139          * Before method resolution,
3140          * if the explicitly specified caller class is not identical with the
3141          * lookup class, or if this lookup object does not have
3142          * <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private access</a>
3143          * privileges, the access fails.
3144          * <p>
3145          * The returned method handle will have
3146          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3147          * the method's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3148          * @param m the reflected method
3149          * @param specialCaller the class nominally calling the method
3150          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected method
3151          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3152          *                                or if the method is {@code static},
3153          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3154          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3155          * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
3156          */
3157         public MethodHandle unreflectSpecial(Method m, Class<?> specialCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3158             checkSpecialCaller(specialCaller, m.getDeclaringClass());
3159             Lookup specialLookup = this.in(specialCaller);
3160             MemberName method = new MemberName(m, true);
3161             assert(method.isMethod());
3162             // ignore m.isAccessible:  this is a new kind of access
3163             return specialLookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(REF_invokeSpecial, method.getDeclaringClass(), method, findBoundCallerLookup(method));
3164         }
3165 
3166         /**
3167          * Produces a method handle for a reflected constructor.
3168          * The type of the method handle will be that of the constructor,
3169          * with the return type changed to the declaring class.
3170          * The method handle will perform a {@code newInstance} operation,
3171          * creating a new instance of the constructor's class on the
3172          * arguments passed to the method handle.
3173          * <p>
3174          * If the constructor's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3175          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3176          * <p>
3177          * The returned method handle will have
3178          * {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity} if and only if
3179          * the constructor's variable arity modifier bit ({@code 0x0080}) is set.
3180          * <p>
3181          * If the returned method handle is invoked, the constructor's class will
3182          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3183          * @param c the reflected constructor
3184          * @return a method handle which can invoke the reflected constructor
3185          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3186          *                                or if the method's variable arity modifier bit
3187          *                                is set and {@code asVarargsCollector} fails
3188          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3189          */
3190         public MethodHandle unreflectConstructor(Constructor<?> c) throws IllegalAccessException {
3191             MemberName ctor = new MemberName(c);
3192             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructorOrStaticInitMethod());
3193             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3194             Lookup lookup = c.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3195             if (ctor.isObjectConstructor()) {
3196                 assert(ctor.getReturnType() == void.class);
3197                 return lookup.getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor);
3198             } else {
3199                 // static init factory is a static method
3200                 assert(ctor.isMethod() && ctor.getReturnType() == ctor.getDeclaringClass() && ctor.getReferenceKind() == REF_invokeStatic);
3201                 assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // must not be caller-sensitive
3202                 return lookup.getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(ctor.getReferenceKind(), ctor.getDeclaringClass(), ctor, lookup);
3203             }
3204         }
