3206         /**
3207          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a reflected field.
3208          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
3209          * value type.
3210          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take no arguments.
3211          * Otherwise, its single argument will be the instance containing
3212          * the field.
3213          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3214          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3215          * <p>
3216          * If the field is static, and
3217          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3218          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3219          * @param f the reflected field
3220          * @return a method handle which can load values from the reflected field
3221          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3222          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3223          */
3224         public MethodHandle unreflectGetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3225             return unreflectField(f, false);
3226         }
3227 
3228         /**
3229          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a reflected field.
3230          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3231          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take a single
3232          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
3233          * Otherwise, the two arguments will be the instance containing
3234          * the field, and the value to be stored.
3235          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3236          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3237          * <p>
3238          * If the field is {@code final}, write access will not be
3239          * allowed and access checking will fail, except under certain
3240          * narrow circumstances documented for {@link Field#set Field.set}.
3241          * A method handle is returned only if a corresponding call to
3242          * the {@code Field} object's {@code set} method could return
3243          * normally.  In particular, fields which are both {@code static}
3244          * and {@code final} may never be set.
3245          * <p>
3246          * If the field is {@code static}, and
3247          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3248          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3249          * @param f the reflected field
3250          * @return a method handle which can store values into the reflected field
3251          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3252          *         or if the field is {@code final} and write access
3253          *         is not enabled on the {@code Field} object
3254          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3255          */
3256         public MethodHandle unreflectSetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3257             return unreflectField(f, true);
3258         }
3259 
3260         private MethodHandle unreflectField(Field f, boolean isSetter) throws IllegalAccessException {
3261             MemberName field = new MemberName(f, isSetter);
3262             if (isSetter && field.isFinal()) {
3263                 if (field.isStatic()) {
3264                     throw field.makeAccessException("static final field has no write access", this);
3265                 } else if (field.getDeclaringClass().isHidden()){
3266                     throw field.makeAccessException("final field in a hidden class has no write access", this);
3267                 }
3268             }
3269             assert(isSetter
3270                     ? MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(field.getReferenceKind())
3271                     : MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(field.getReferenceKind()));
3272             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3273             Lookup lookup = f.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3274             return lookup.getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(field.getReferenceKind(), f.getDeclaringClass(), field);
3275         }
3276 
3277         /**
3278          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a reflected field {@code f}
3279          * of type {@code T} declared in a class of type {@code R}.
3280          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code T}.
3281          * If the field is non-static the VarHandle has one coordinate type,
3282          * {@code R}.  Otherwise, the field is static, and the VarHandle has no
3283          * coordinate types.
3284          * <p>
3285          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
3286          * class, regardless of the value of the field's {@code accessible}
3287          * flag.
3288          * <p>
3289          * If the field is static, and if the returned VarHandle is operated
3290          * on, the field's declaring class will be initialized, if it has not
3291          * already been initialized.
3292          * <p>
3293          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3294          * the following conditions:
3295          * <ul>
3296          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
3297          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
3298          *     modes are unsupported.
3299          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
3300          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3301          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
3302          *     access modes are unsupported.
3303          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3304          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3305          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3306          *     unsupported.
3307          * </ul>
3308          * <p>
3309          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
3310          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
3311          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3312          * access modes.
3313          * <p>
3314          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3315          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3316          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3317          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3318          * @apiNote
3319          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3320          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3321          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3322          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3323          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3324          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3325          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3326          * unexpectedly fail.
3327          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3328          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3329          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3330          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3331          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3332          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3333          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3334          * details).
3335          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3336          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3337          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3338          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3339          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3340          * @param f the reflected field, with a field of type {@code T}, and
3341          * a declaring class of type {@code R}
3342          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields or a static
3343          * field
3344          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3345          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3346          * @since 9
3347          */
3348         public VarHandle unreflectVarHandle(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3349             MemberName getField = new MemberName(f, false);
3350             MemberName putField = new MemberName(f, true);
3351             return getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(getField.getReferenceKind(), putField.getReferenceKind(),
3352                                                       f.getDeclaringClass(), getField, putField);
3353         }
3354 
3355         /**
3356          * Cracks a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3357          * created by this lookup object or a similar one.
3358          * Security and access checks are performed to ensure that this lookup object
3359          * is capable of reproducing the target method handle.
3360          * This means that the cracking may fail if target is a direct method handle
3361          * but was created by an unrelated lookup object.
3362          * This can happen if the method handle is <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#callsens">caller sensitive</a>
3363          * and was created by a lookup object for a different class.
3364          * @param target a direct method handle to crack into symbolic reference components
3365          * @return a symbolic reference which can be used to reconstruct this method handle from this lookup object
3366          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3367          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3368          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the target is not a direct method handle or if access checking fails
3369          * @throws    NullPointerException if the target is {@code null}
3370          * @see MethodHandleInfo
3371          * @since 1.8
3372          */
3373         public MethodHandleInfo revealDirect(MethodHandle target) {
3374             if (!target.isCrackable()) {
3375                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("not a direct method handle");
3376             }
3377             MemberName member = target.internalMemberName();
3378             Class<?> defc = member.getDeclaringClass();
3379             byte refKind = member.getReferenceKind();
3380             assert(MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind));
3381             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial && !target.isInvokeSpecial())
3382                 // Devirtualized method invocation is usually formally virtual.
3383                 // To avoid creating extra MemberName objects for this common case,
3384                 // we encode this extra degree of freedom using MH.isInvokeSpecial.
3385                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3386             if (refKind == REF_invokeVirtual && defc.isInterface())
3387                 // Symbolic reference is through interface but resolves to Object method (toString, etc.)
3388                 refKind = REF_invokeInterface;
3389             // Check SM permissions and member access before cracking.
3390             try {
3391                 checkAccess(refKind, defc, member);
3392                 checkSecurityManager(defc, member);
3393             } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) {
3394                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
3395             }
3396             if (allowedModes != TRUSTED && member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3397                 Class<?> callerClass = target.internalCallerClass();
3398                 if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess() || callerClass != lookupClass())
3399                     throw new IllegalArgumentException("method handle is caller sensitive: "+callerClass);
3400             }
3401             // Produce the handle to the results.
3402             return new InfoFromMemberName(this, member, refKind);
3403         }
3404 
3405         /// Helper methods, all package-private.
3406 
3407         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3408             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3409             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3410             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3411             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3412                                             NoSuchFieldException.class);
3413         }
3414 
3415         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3416             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3417             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3418             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3419             checkMethodName(refKind, name);  // NPE check on name
3420             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3421                                             NoSuchMethodException.class);
3422         }
3423 
3424         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, MemberName member) throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3425             checkSymbolicClass(member.getDeclaringClass());  // do this before attempting to resolve
3426             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3427             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3428             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull(),
3429                                             ReflectiveOperationException.class);
3430         }
3431 
3432         MemberName resolveOrNull(byte refKind, MemberName member) {
3433             // do this before attempting to resolve
3434             if (!isClassAccessible(member.getDeclaringClass())) {
3435                 return null;
3436             }
3437             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3438             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3439             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull());
3440         }
3441 
3442         void checkSymbolicClass(Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3443             if (!isClassAccessible(refc)) {
3444                 throw new MemberName(refc).makeAccessException("symbolic reference class is not accessible", this);
3445             }
3446         }
3447 
3448         boolean isClassAccessible(Class<?> refc) {
3449             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3450             Class<?> caller = lookupClassOrNull();
3451             return caller == null || VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, caller, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
3452         }
3453 
3454         /** Check name for an illegal leading "&lt;" character. */
3455         void checkMethodName(byte refKind, String name) throws NoSuchMethodException {
3456             // "<init>" can only be invoked via invokespecial or it's a static init factory
3457             if (name.startsWith("<") && refKind != REF_newInvokeSpecial &&
3458                     !(refKind == REF_invokeStatic && name.equals("<init>"))) {
3459                     throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
3460             }
3461         }
3462 
3463         /**
3464          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3465          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3466          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3467          */
3468         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3469             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3470                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3471                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3472             }
3473             return this;
3474         }
3475 
3476         /**
3477          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3478          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3479          *
3480          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3481          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3482          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3483          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3484          * @since 9
3485          */
3486         @Deprecated(since="14")
3487         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3488             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3489         }
3490 
3491         /**
3492          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3493          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3494          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3495          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3496          *
3497          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3498          * @since 14
3499          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3500          */
3501         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3502             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3503         }
3504 
3505         /**
3506          * Perform necessary <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3507          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3508          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3509          */
3510         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3511             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3512 
3513             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3514             if (smgr == null)  return;
3515 
3516             // Step 1:
3517             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3518             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3519                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3520                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3521             }
3522 
3523             if (m == null) {  // findClass or accessClass
3524                 // Step 2b:
3525                 if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3526                     smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3527                 }
3528                 return;
3529             }
3530 
3531             // Step 2a:
3532             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3533             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3534                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3535             }
3536 
3537             // Step 3:
3538             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3539             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3540                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3541             }
3542         }
3543 
3544         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3545             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3546             String message;
3547             if (m.isObjectConstructor())
3548                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3549             else if (!m.isMethod())
3550                 message = "expected a method";
3551             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3552                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3553             else
3554                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3555             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3556         }
3557 
3558         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3559             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3560             String message;
3561             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3562                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3563             else
3564                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3565             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3566         }
3567 
3568         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3569         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3570             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3571                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3572                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3573             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3574             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3575             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3576             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3577                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3578                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3579                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3580                     refc.isArray()) {
3581                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3582                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3583                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3584                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3585                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3586                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3587                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3588                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3589                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3590                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3591                 // requested array type.
3592                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3593                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3594                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3595             }
3596             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3597                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3598                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3599             }
3600             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3601                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3602                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3603             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3604             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3605                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3606                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3607                     return;
3608             } else {
3609                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3610                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3611                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3612                     return;
3613             }
3614             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3615         }
3616 
3617         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3618             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3619             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3620             // check the class first:
3621             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3622                                (defc == refc ||
3623                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3624             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3625                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3626                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3627                            (defc == refc ||
3628                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3629             }
3630             if (!classOK)
3631                 return "class is not public";
3632             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3633                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3634             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3635                 return "member is private";
3636             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3637                 return "member is protected";
3638             return "member is private to package";
3639         }
3640 
3641         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3642             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3643             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3644             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3645                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3646                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3647                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3648                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3649                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3650         }
3651 
3652         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3653             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3654             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3655             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3656                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3657                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3658                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3659                 return false;
3660             return true;
3661         }
3662         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3663             assert(!method.isStatic());
3664             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3665             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3666                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3667             }
3668             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3669             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3670             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3671             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3672             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3673             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3674         }
3675 
3676         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3677         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3678             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3679             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3680             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3681         }
3682         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3683         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3684             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3685             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3686             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3687         }
3688         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3689         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3690             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3691             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3692             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3693         }
3694         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3695         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3696                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3697                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3698                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3699             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3700             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3701             if (checkSecurity)
3702                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3703             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3704 
3705             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3706                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3707                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3708                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3709                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3710                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3711 
3712                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3713                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3714                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3715                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3716                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3717                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3718                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3719                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3720                 MemberName m2;
3721                 do {
3722                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3723                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3724                                         method.getName(),
3725                                         method.getMethodType(),
3726                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3727                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3728                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3729                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3730                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3731                 method = m2;
3732                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3733                 // redo basic checks
3734                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3735             }
3736             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3737             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3738             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3739             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3740                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3741                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3742             }
3743             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3744             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3745             return mh;
3746         }
3747         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3748                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3749             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3750                 return mh;
3751 
3752             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3753             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3754             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3755                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3756 
3757             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3758             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3759             return cbmh;
3760         }
3761 
3762         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3763         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3764             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3765             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3766         }
3767         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3768         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3769             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3770             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3771         }
3772         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3773         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3774                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3775             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3776             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3777             if (checkSecurity)
3778                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3779             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3780             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3781                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3782             if (doRestrict)
3783                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3784             return dmh;
3785         }
3786         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3787                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3788                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3789             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3790             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3791         }
3792         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3793                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3794                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3795             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3796             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3797         }
3798         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3799                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3800                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3801             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3802             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3803             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3804             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3805 
3806             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3807             if (checkSecurity)
3808                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3809 
3810             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3811                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3812                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3813                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3814                 // only required for non-final fields
3815                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3816                 if (checkSecurity)
3817                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3818             }
3819 
3820             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3821                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3822             if (doRestrict) {
3823                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3824                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3825                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3826                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3827                 }
3828                 refc = lookupClass();
3829             }
3830             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3831                                              this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.getDeclaringClass().isHidden());
3832         }
3833         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3834         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3835             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3836             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3837         }
3838         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3839         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3840             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3841             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3842         }
3843         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3844         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3845                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3846             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructor());
3847             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3848             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3849             if (checkSecurity)
3850                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3851             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3852             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3853         }
3854 
3855         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3856          */
3857         /*non-public*/
3858         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3859                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3860             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3861                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3862             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3863             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3864             if (mh != null) {
3865                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3866                 return mh;
3867             }
3868             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3869                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3870                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3871                 if (mh != null) {
3872                     return mh;
3873                 }
3874             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3875                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3876                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3877                 if (mh != null) {
3878                     return mh;
3879                 }
3880             }
3881             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3882             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3883             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3884                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3885                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3886                 if (key != null) {
3887                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3888                 }
3889                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3890                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3891                 }
3892             }
3893             return mh;
3894         }
3895         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3896             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3897                 return false;
3898             }
3899             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3900                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3901                     !member.isPublic() ||
3902                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3903                 return false;
3904             }
3905             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3906             if (loader != null) {
3907                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3908                 boolean found = false;
3909                 while (sysl != null) {
3910                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3911                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3912                 }
3913                 if (!found) {
3914                     return false;
3915                 }
3916             }
3917             try {
3918                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3919                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3920                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3921                     return false;
3922                 }
3923                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3924             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3925                 return false;
3926             }
3927             return true;
3928         }
3929         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3930                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3931             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3932                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3933             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3934                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3935             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3936                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3937             }
3938             // oops
3939             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3940         }
3941 
3942         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3943     }
3944 
3945     /**
3946      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3947      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3948      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3949      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
3950      *
3951      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
3952      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
3953      *
3954      * @param arrayClass an array type
3955      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
3956      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3957      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
3958      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
3959      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
3960      * @since 9
3961      */
3962     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3963         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
3964             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
3965         }
3966         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
3967                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
3968         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
3969     }
3970 
3971     /**
3972      * Produces a method handle returning the length of an array,
3973      * as if by the {@code arraylength} bytecode.
3974      * The type of the method handle will have {@code int} as return type,
3975      * and its sole argument will be the array type.
3976      *
3977      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a {@code null}
3978      * array reference, a {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown.
3979      *
3980      * @param arrayClass an array type
3981      * @return a method handle which can retrieve the length of an array of the given array type
3982      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3983      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3984      * @jvms 6.5 {@code arraylength} Instruction
3985      * @since 9
3986      */
3987     public static MethodHandle arrayLength(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3988         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.LENGTH);
3989     }

3991     /**
3992      * Produces a method handle giving read access to elements of an array,
3993      * as if by the {@code aaload} bytecode.
3994      * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the array's
3995      * element type.  Its first argument will be the array type,
3996      * and the second will be {@code int}.
3997      *
3998      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3999      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4000      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4001      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4002      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4003      * the length of the array.
4004      *
4005      * @param arrayClass an array type
4006      * @return a method handle which can load values from the given array type
4007      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4008      * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4009      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aaload} Instruction
4010      */
4011     public static MethodHandle arrayElementGetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4012         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.GET);
4013     }

4015     /**
4016      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
4017      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
4018      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
4019      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
4020      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
4021      *
4022      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
4023      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4024      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4025      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4026      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4027      * the length of the array.
4028      *
4029      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
4030      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
4031      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4032      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4033      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
4034      */
4035     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4036         if (arrayClass.isInlineClass()) {
4037             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
4038         }
4039         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
4040     }
4041 
4042     /**
4043      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
4044      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
4045      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4046      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4047      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
4048      * <p>
4049      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
4050      * the following conditions:
4051      * <ul>
4052      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
4053      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
4054      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
4055      *     modes are unsupported.
4056      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code boolean},
4057      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
4058      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
4059      *     unsupported.
4060      * </ul>
4061      * <p>
4062      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
4063      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
4064      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4065      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4066      *
4067      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
4068      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4069      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4070      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4071      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4072      * the length of the array.
4073      *
4074      * @apiNote
4075      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
4076      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
4077      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
4078      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
4079      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
4080      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
4081      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
4082      * unexpectedly fail.
4083      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
4084      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
4085      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
4086      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
4087      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
4088      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
4089      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
4090      * details).
4091      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
4092      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4093      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4094      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4095      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4096      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4097      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4098      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4099      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4100      * @since 9
4101      */
4102     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4103         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4104     }
4105 
4106     /**
4107      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4108      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4109      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4110      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4111      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4112      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4113      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4114      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4115      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4116      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4117      * <p>
4118      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4119      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4120      * {@code double}.
4121      * <p>
4122      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4123      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4124      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4125      * of {@code T}.
4126      * <p>
4127      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4128      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4129      * with the array and index.
4130      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4131      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4132      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4133      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4134      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4135      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4136      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4137      * <ul>
4138      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4139      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4140      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4141      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4142      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4143      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4144      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4145      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4146      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4147      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4148      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4149      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4150      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4151      * </ul>
4152      * <p>
4153      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4154      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4155      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4156      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4157      * <pre>{@code
4158      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4159      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4160      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4161      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4162      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4163      * }</pre>
4164      * <p>
4165      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4166      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4167      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4168      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4169      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4170      * type {@code T}
4171      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4172      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4173      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4174      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4175      * array class
4176      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4177      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4178      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4179      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4180      * @since 9
4181      */
4182     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4183                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4184         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4185         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4186                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4187     }
4188 
4189     /**
4190      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4191      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4192      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4193      * {@code long[]}.
4194      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4195      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4196      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4197      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4198      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4199      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4200      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4201      * <p>
4202      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4203      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4204      * {@code double}.
4205      * <p>
4206      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4207      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4208      * <p>
4209      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4210      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4211      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4212      * {@code T}.
4213      * <p>
4214      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4215      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4216      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4217      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4218      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4219      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4220      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4221      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4222      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4223      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4224      * <ul>
4225      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4226      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4227      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4228      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4229      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4230      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4231      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4232      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4233      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4234      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4235      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4236      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4237      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4238      * </ul>
4239      * <p>
4240      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4241      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4242      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4243      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4244      * <pre>{@code
4245      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4246      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4247      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4248      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4249      * }</pre>
4250      * <p>
4251      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4252      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4253      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4254      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4255      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4256      * type {@code T}
4257      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4258      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4259      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4260      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4261      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4262      * array class
4263      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4264      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4265      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4266      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4267      * @since 9
4268      */
4269     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4270                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4271         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4272         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4273                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4274     }

4277     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4278 
4279     /**
4280      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4281      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4282      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4283      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4284      * arguments:
4285      * <ul>
4286      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4287      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4288      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4289      * </ul>
4290      * <p>
4291      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4292      * the indicated {@code type}.
4293      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4294      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4295      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4296      * <p>
4297      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4298      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4299      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4300      * the final parameter.
4301      * <p>
4302      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4303      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4304      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4305      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4306      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4307      * <p>
4308      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4309      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4310 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4311 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4312 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4313 return invoker;
4314      * }</pre></blockquote>
4315      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4316      * @param type the desired target type
4317      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4318      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4319      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4320      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4321      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4322      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4323      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4324      */
4325     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4326         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4327             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4328         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4329         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4330     }
4331 
4332     /**
4333      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4334      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4335      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4336      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4337      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4338      * <p>
4339      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4340      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4341      *
4342      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4343      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4344      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4345      * of unknown types.
4346      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4347      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4348      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4349      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4350      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4351      * is unknown.)
4352      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4353      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4354      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4355      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4356      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4357      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4358      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4359      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4360      * <p>
4361      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4362      * @param type the desired target type
4363      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4364      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4365      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4366      */
4367     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4368         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4369     }
4370 
4371     /**
4372      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4373      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4374      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4375      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4376      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4377      * <p>
4378      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4379      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4380      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4381      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4382      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4383      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4384      * <p>
4385      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4386      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4387      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4388      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4389      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4390      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4391      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4392      * of the same arity as the general type.
4393      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4394      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4395      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4396      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4397      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4398      * <p>
4399      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4400      * @param type the desired target type
4401      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4402      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4403      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4404      */
4405     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4406         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4407     }

4409     /**
4410      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4411      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4412      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4413      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4414      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4415      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4416      *
4417      * @param accessMode the VarHandle access mode
4418      * @param type the desired target type
4419      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking an access mode method of
4420      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.
4421      * @since 9
4422      */
4423     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {
4424         return type.invokers().varHandleMethodExactInvoker(accessMode);
4425     }

4427     /**
4428      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4429      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4430      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4431      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4432      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4433      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4434      * <p>
4435      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the
4436      * desired given type, the invoker will apply reference casts as necessary
4437      * and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by
4438      * {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.  Similarly, the return value will be
4439      * converted as necessary.
4440      * <p>
4441      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more
4442      * efficient): {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(VarHandle.class, accessMode.name(), type)}
4443      *
4444      * @param accessMode the VarHandle access mode
4445      * @param type the desired target type
4446      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking an access mode method of
4447      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is convertible to the given
4448      *         type.
4449      * @since 9
4450      */
4451     public static MethodHandle varHandleInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {
4452         return type.invokers().varHandleMethodInvoker(accessMode);

4458     }

4460      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4461 
4462     /**
4463      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4464      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4465      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4466      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4467      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4468      * <p>
4469      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4470      * <p>
4471      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4472      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4473      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4474      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4475      * <ul>
4476      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4477      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4478      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4479      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4480      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4481      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4482      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4483      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4484      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4485      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4486      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4487      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4488      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4489      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4490      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4491      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4492      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4493      *     the low-order bit.
4494      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4495      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4496      * </ul>
4497      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4498      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4499      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4500      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4501      *           necessary return value conversions
4502      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4503      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4504      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4505      */
4506     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4507         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4508         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4509         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4510         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4511         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4512             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4513         }
4514         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4515     }
4516 
4517     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4518         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4519             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4520         }
4521     }
4522 
4523     /**
4524      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4525      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4526      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4527      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4528      * <p>
4529      * The given array controls the reordering.
4530      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4531      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
