4532      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4533      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4534      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4535      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4536      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4537      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4538      * <p>
4539      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4540      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4541      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4542      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4543      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4544      * type of the original target.
4545      * <p>
4546      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4547      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4548      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4549      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4550      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4551      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4552      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4553      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4554 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4555 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4556 ...
4557 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4558 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4559 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4560 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4561 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4562 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4563 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4564 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
4565 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
4566 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
4567 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
4568 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
4569      * }</pre></blockquote>
4570      * <p>
4571      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4572      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4573      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
4574      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4575      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
4576      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
4577      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
4578      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
4579      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
4580      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
4581      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
4582      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
4583      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
4584      */
4585     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
4586         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
4587         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4588         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
4589         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
4590         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
4591         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4592         LambdaForm form = result.form;
4593         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
4594         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
4595         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
4596         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
4597         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
4598         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
4599             if (ddIdx > 0) {
4600                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
4601                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
4602                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
4603                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
4604                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
4605                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
4606                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
4607                 boolean killFirst = false;
4608                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4609                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4610                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4611                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4612                 }
4613                 if (!killFirst) {
4614                     srcPos = dstPos;
4615                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4616                 }
4617                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4618                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4619                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4620                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4621                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4622                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4623                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4624             } else {
4625                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4626                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4627                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4628                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4629                     insPos += 1;
4630                 }
4631                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4632                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4633                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4634                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4635                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4636                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4637                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4638                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4639             }
4640             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4641         }
4642         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4643         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4644         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4645         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4646             return result;
4647         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4648     }
4649 
4650     /**
4651      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4652      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
4653      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4654      * Otherwise, return zero.
4655      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4656      */
4657     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4658         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4659         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4660             long mask = 0;
4661             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4662                 int arg = reorder[i];
4663                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4664                     return reorder.length;
4665                 }
4666                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4667                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4668                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4669                 }
4670                 mask |= bit;
4671             }
4672             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4673                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4674                 return 0;
4675             }
4676             // find first zero
4677             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4678             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4679             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4680             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4681                 return 0;
4682             }
4683             return ~zeroPos;
4684         } else {
4685             // same algorithm, different bit set
4686             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4687             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4688                 int arg = reorder[i];
4689                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4690                     return reorder.length;
4691                 }
4692                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4693                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4694                 }
4695                 mask.set(arg);
4696             }
4697             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4698             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4699             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4700                 return 0;
4701             }
4702             return ~zeroPos;
4703         }
4704     }
4705 
4706     static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4707         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4708             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4709                     oldType, newType);
4710         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4711             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4712             boolean bad = false;
4713             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4714                 int i = reorder[j];
4715                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4716                     bad = true; break;
4717                 }
4718                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4719                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4720                 if (src != dst)
4721                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4722                             oldType, newType);
4723             }
4724             if (!bad)  return true;
4725         }
4726         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4727     }
4728 
4729     /**
4730      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4731      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4732      * <p>
4733      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4734      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4735      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4736      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4737      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4738      * @param value the value to return
4739      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4740      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4741      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4742      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4743      */
4744     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4745         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4746             if (type == void.class)
4747                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4748             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4749             value = w.convert(value, type);
4750             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4751                 return zero(w, type);
4752             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4753         } else {
4754             if (value == null)
4755                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4756             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4757         }
4758     }
4759 
4760     /**
4761      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4762      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4763      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4764      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4765      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4766      */
4767     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4768         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4769         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4770         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4771         if (ident == null) {
4772             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4773         }
4774         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4775             return ident;
4776         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4777         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4778         return makeIdentity(type);
4779     }
4780 
4781     /**
4782      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4783      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4784      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4785      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4786      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4787      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4788      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4789      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4790      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4791      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4792      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4793      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4794      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4795      * @since 9
4796      */
4797     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4798         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4799         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4800             return zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type);
4801         } else if (type.isInlineClass()) {
4802             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
4803         } else {
4804             return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4805         }
4806     }
4807 
4808     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4809         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4810     }
4811 
4812     /**
4813      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4814      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4815      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4816      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4817      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4818      *
4819      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4820      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4821      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4822      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4823      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4824      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4825      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4826      * @since 9
4827      */
4828     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4829         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4830         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4831     }
4832 
4833     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4834     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4835         MethodType mtype = MethodType.methodType(ptype, ptype);
4836         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4837         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4838     }
4839 
4840     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4841         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4842         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4843         if (zero == null) {
4844             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4845         }
4846         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4847             return zero;
4848         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4849         return makeZero(rtype);
4850     }
4851     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4852     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4853         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4854         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4855         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4856     }
4857 
4858     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4859         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4860         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4861         if (prev != null) return prev;
4862         return cache[pos] = value;
4863     }
4864 
4865     /**
4866      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4867      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4868      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4869      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4870      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4871      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4872      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4873      * and calls the original target.
4874      * <p>
4875      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4876      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4877      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4878      * <p>
4879      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4880      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4881      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4882      * <p>
4883      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4884      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4885      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4886      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4887      * <p>
4888      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4889      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4890      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4891      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4892      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4893      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4894      *         before calling the original method handle
4895      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4896      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4897      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4898      *         is the length of the values array.
4899      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4900      *         type.
4901      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4902      */
4903     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4904         int insCount = values.length;
4905         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4906         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4907         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4908         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4909             Object value = values[i];
4910             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4911             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4912                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4913             } else {
4914                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4915                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4916             }
4917         }
4918         return result;
4919     }
4920 
4921     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4922                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4923         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4924         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4925         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4926         switch (w) {
4927         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4928         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4929         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4930         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4931         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4932         }
4933     }
4934 
4935     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4936         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4937         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4938         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4939         if (inargs < 0)
4940             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4941         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4942             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4943         return oldType.ptypes();
4944     }
4945 
4946     /**
4947      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4948      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4949      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4950      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4951      * at some given position.
4952      * <p>
4953      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4954      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4955      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4956      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4957      * they will come after.
4958      * <p>
4959      * <b>Example:</b>
4960      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4961 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4962 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4963 ...
4964 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4965   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4966 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4967 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
4968 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
4969 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
4970 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
4971      * }</pre></blockquote>
4972      * <p>
4973      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4974      * <blockquote><pre>
4975      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
4976      * </pre></blockquote>
4977      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4978      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4979      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4980      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4981      *         before calling the original method handle
4982      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4983      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
4984      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4985      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4986      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
4987      */
4988     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4989         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
4990     }
4991 
4992     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
4993         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
4994     }
4995 
4996     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4997         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
4998         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
4999         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
5000         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
5001         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5002         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
5003         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
5004         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
5005             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
5006         }
5007         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5008         return result;
5009     }
5010 
5011     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
5012         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
5013         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
5014         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
5015         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
5016         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
5017             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
5018                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
5019                     );
5020         return dropped;
5021     }
5022 
5023     /**
5024      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
5025      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
5026      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
5027      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
5028      * at some given position.
5029      * <p>
5030      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
5031      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
5032      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
5033      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
5034      * they will come after.
5035      * @apiNote
5036      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5037 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5038 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5039 ...
5040 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5041   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5042 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5043 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
5044 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5045 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
5046 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5047 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
5048 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
5049 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
5050 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
5051      * }</pre></blockquote>
5052      * <p>
5053      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
5054      * <blockquote><pre>
5055      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
5056      * </pre></blockquote>
5057      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
5058      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
5059      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
5060      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
5061      *         before calling the original method handle
5062      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
5063      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
5064      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
5065      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5066      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
5067      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5068      */
5069     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
5070         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
5071     }
5072 
5073     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
5074     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
5075                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
5076         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
5077         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
5078         int match = oldTypes.size();
5079         if (skip != 0) {
5080             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
5081                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
5082             }
5083             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
5084             match -= skip;
5085         }
5086         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
5087         int add = addTypes.size();
5088         if (pos != 0) {
5089             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
5090                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
5091             }
5092             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
5093             add -= pos;
5094             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5095         }
5096         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
5097         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
5098             if (nullOnFailure) {
5099                 return null;
5100             }
5101             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
5102         }
5103         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
5104         add -= match;
5105         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5106         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5107         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
5108         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5109         if (add > 0) {
5110             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
5111         }
5112         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
5113         if (pos > 0) {
5114             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
5115         }
5116         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5117         return adapter;
5118     }
5119 
5120     /**
5121      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
5122      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
5123      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
5124      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
5125      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
5126      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5127      * <p>
5128      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
5129      * <p>
5130      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
5131      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
5132      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
5133      * {@code newTypes}.
5134      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
5135      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
5136      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
5137      * sub-list.
5138      * </ul>
5139      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
5140      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
5141      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5142      *
5143      * @apiNote
5144      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
5145      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
5146      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5147 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5148 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5149 ...
5150 ...
5151 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
5152 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5153 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
5154 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
5155 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
5156     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
5157 else
5158     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
5159 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
5160 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
5161      * }</pre></blockquote>
5162      * @param target the method handle to adapt
5163      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
5164      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
5165      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
5166      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
5167      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5168      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
5169      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5170      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
5171      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
5172      *         {@code pos}.
5173      * @since 9
5174      */
5175     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
5176         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
5177         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
5178         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
5179     }
5180 
5181     /**
5182      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5183      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
5184      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
5185      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
5186      * <p>
5187      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
5188      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
5189      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
5190      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
5191      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
5192      * <p>
5193      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
5194      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
5195      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
5196      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
5197      * <p>
5198      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
5199      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
5200      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
5201      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
5202      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5203      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
5204      * parameter type of the target.
5205      * <p>
5206      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
5207      * (null or not)
5208      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
5209      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5210      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5211 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5212 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5213 ...
5214 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5215   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5216 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5217   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
5218 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5219 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
5220 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
5221 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
5222 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
5223 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
5224 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
5225      * }</pre></blockquote>
5226      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5227      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5228      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
5229      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
5230      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
5231      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
5232      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
5233      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
5234      * the resulting adapter.
5235      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5236      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
5237      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
5238      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
5239      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
5240      * }
5241      * }</pre></blockquote>
5242      * <p>
5243      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5244      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5245      *
5246      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
5247      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
5248      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
5249      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
5250      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
5251      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
5252      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
5253      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
5254      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
5255      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5256      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5257      */
5258     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
5259         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
5260         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
5261         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
5262         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
5263         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5264 
5265         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
5266         int index = 0;
5267         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
5268         MethodHandle filter = null;
5269 
5270         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
5271         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
5272         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
5273             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
5274             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
5275 
5276             // flush changes on update
5277             if (filter != newFilter) {
5278                 if (filter != null) {
5279                     if (index > 1) {
5280                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5281                     } else {
5282                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5283                     }
5284                 }
5285                 filter = newFilter;
5286                 index = 0;
5287             }
5288 
5289             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
5290             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
5291         }
5292         if (index > 1) {
5293             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5294         } else if (index == 1) {
5295             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5296         }
5297         return adapter;
5298     }
5299 
5300     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
5301         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
5302         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5303         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
5304         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5305 
5306         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
5307         for (int pos : positions) {
5308             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
5309         }
5310         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
5311 
5312         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
5313         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5314     }
5315 
5316     /*non-public*/
5317     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5318         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
5319         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5320         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5321         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5322         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5323         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
5324         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
5325         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5326         return result;
5327     }
5328 
5329     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
5330         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5331         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
5332         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
5333             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
5334     }
5335 
5336     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5337         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5338         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5339         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
5340             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
5341             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5342     }
5343 
5344     /**
5345      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5346      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
5347      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
5348      * filter function.
5349      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
5350      * <p>
5351      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
5352      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
5353      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
5354      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
5355      * not passed to the filter.
5356      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
5357      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
5358      * passed to the adapter.
5359      * <p>
5360      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
5361      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
5362      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5363      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5364      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
5365      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
5366      * <p>
5367      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
5368      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
5369      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5370      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5371 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5372 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5373 ...
5374 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
5375   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
5376 
5377 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
5378 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
5379 
5380 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
5381 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
5382 
5383 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
5384 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
5385 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
5386              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5387 
5388 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
5389 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
5390              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5391 
5392 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
5393 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
5394              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
5395      * }</pre></blockquote>
5396      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5397      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5398      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
5399      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
5400      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
5401      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
5402      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
5403      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
5404      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
5405      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
5406      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
5407      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5408      * T target(A...,V,C...);
5409      * V filter(B...);
5410      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5411      *   V v = filter(b...);
5412      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
5413      * }
5414      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
5415      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
5416      * V filter2();
5417      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
5418      *   V v = filter2();
5419      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
5420      * }
5421      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5422      * T target3(A...,C...);
5423      * void filter3(B...);
5424      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5425      *   filter3(b...);
5426      *   return target3(a...,c...);
5427      * }
5428      * }</pre></blockquote>
5429      * <p>
5430      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
5431      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
5432      * steps as follows:
5433      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5434      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
5435      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
5436      * }</pre></blockquote>
5437      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
5438      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
5439      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
5440      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
5441      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
5442      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
5443      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
5444      * <p>
5445      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5446      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5447      *
5448      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
5449      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
5450      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
5451      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
5452      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
5453      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5454      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
5455      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
5456      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
5457      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5458      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5459      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
5460      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
5461      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
5462      */
5463     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5464         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
5465         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
5466         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5467         LambdaForm lform;
5468         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
5469             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
5470             if (lform != null) {
5471                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5472             }
5473         }
5474         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
5475         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5476     }
5477 
5478     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5479         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5480         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5481         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
5482         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
5483         if (rtype == void.class) {
5484             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5485         }
5486         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
5487             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5488         }
5489         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5490     }
5491 
5492     /**
5493      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
5494      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
5495      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
5496      * <p>
5497      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
5498      * its only argument.
5499      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
5500      * <p>
5501      * The return type of the filter
5502      * replaces the return type of the target
5503      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5504      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5505      * return type of the target.
5506      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5507      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5508 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5509 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5510 ...
5511 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5512   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5513 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5514   "length", methodType(int.class));
5515 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
5516 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
5517 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
5518      * }</pre></blockquote>
5519      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
5520      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
5521      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
5522      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
5523      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
5524      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5525      * T target(A...);
5526      * V filter(T);
5527      * V adapter(A... a) {
5528      *   T t = target(a...);
5529      *   return filter(t);
5530      * }
5531      * // and if the target has a void return:
5532      * void target2(A...);
5533      * V filter2();
5534      * V adapter2(A... a) {
5535      *   target2(a...);
5536      *   return filter2();
5537      * }
5538      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5539      * T target3(A...);
5540      * void filter3(V);
5541      * void adapter3(A... a) {
5542      *   T t = target3(a...);
5543      *   filter3(t);
5544      * }
5545      * }</pre></blockquote>
5546      * <p>
5547      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5548      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5549      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
5550      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
5551      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
5552      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5553      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
5554      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
5555      */
5556     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5557         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5558         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5559         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
5560         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5561         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
5562         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
5563         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5564         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5565         return result;
5566     }
5567 
5568     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
5569         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
5570         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
5571         if (filterValues == 0
5572                 ? (rtype != void.class)
5573                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
5574             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5575     }
5576 
5577     /**
5578      * Filter the return value of a target method handle with a filter function. The filter function is
5579      * applied to the return value of the original handle; if the filter specifies more than one parameters,
5580      * then any remaining parameter is appended to the adapter handle. In other words, the adaptation works
5581      * as follows:
5582      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5583      * T target(A...)
5584      * V filter(B... , T)
5585      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5586      *     T t = target(a...);
5587      *     return filter(b..., t);
5588      * }</pre></blockquote>
5589      * <p>
5590      * If the filter handle is a unary function, then this method behaves like {@link #filterReturnValue(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5591      *
5592      * @param target the target method handle
5593      * @param filter the filter method handle
5594      * @return the adapter method handle
5595      */
5596     /* package */ static MethodHandle collectReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5597         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5598         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5599         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5600         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().collectReturnValueForm(filterType.basicType());
5601         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5602         if (filterType.parameterList().size() > 1) {
5603             for (int i = 0 ; i < filterType.parameterList().size() - 1 ; i++) {
5604                 newType = newType.appendParameterTypes(filterType.parameterType(i));
5605             }
5606         }
5607         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5608         return result;
5609     }
5610 
5611     /**
5612      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5613      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
5614      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
5615      * sequence of arguments.
5616      * <p>
5617      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
5618      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
5619      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
5620      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
5621      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
5622      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
5623      * arguments.
5624      * <p>
5625      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
5626      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
5627      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
5628      * of the combiner.
5629      * <p>
5630      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
5631      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
5632      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
5633      * <p>
5634      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5635      * first parameter type is dropped,
5636      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5637      * <p>
5638      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5639      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5640      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5641      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5642      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5643      * target.)
5644      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5645      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5646 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5647 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5648 ...
5649 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5650   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5651     .bindTo(System.out);
5652 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5653   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5654 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5655 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5656 // also prints "boo":
5657 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5658      * }</pre></blockquote>
5659      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5660      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5661      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5662      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5663      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5664      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5665      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5666      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5667      * and arguments.
5668      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5669      * // there are N arguments in A...
5670      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5671      * V combiner(A...);
5672      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5673      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5674      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5675      * }
5676      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5677      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5678      * void combiner2(A...);
5679      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5680      *   combiner2(a...);
5681      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5682      * }
5683      * }</pre></blockquote>
5684      * <p>
5685      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5686      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5687      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5688      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5689      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5690      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5691      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5692      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5693      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5694      *          of the target
5695      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5696      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5697      */
5698     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5699         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5700     }
5701 
5702     /**
5703      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5704      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5705      * before the folded arguments.
5706      * <p>
5707      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5708      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5709      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5710      * 0.
5711      *
5712      * @apiNote Example:
5713      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5714     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5715     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5716     ...
5717     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5718     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5719     .bindTo(System.out);
5720     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5721     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5722     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5723     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5724     // also prints "jum":
5725     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5726      * }</pre></blockquote>
5727      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5728      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5729      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5730      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5731      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5732      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5733      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5734      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5735      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5736      * respectively.
5737      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5738      * // there are N arguments in A...
5739      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5740      * V combiner(A...);
5741      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5742      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5743      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5744      * }
5745      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5746      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5747      * void combiner2(A...);
5748      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5749      *   combiner2(a...);
5750      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5751      * }
5752      * }</pre></blockquote>
5753      * <p>
5754      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5755      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5756      *
5757      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5758      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5759      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5760      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5761      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5762      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5763      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5764      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5765      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5766      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5767      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5768      *
5769      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5770      * @since 9
5771      */
5772     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5773         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5774         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5775         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5776         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5777         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5778         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5779         MethodType newType = targetType;
5780         if (!dropResult) {
5781             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5782         }
5783         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5784         return result;
5785     }
5786 
5787     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5788         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5789         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5790         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5791         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5792         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5793         if (ok) {
5794             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5795                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5796                     ok = false;
5797                     break;
5798                 }
5799             }
5800         }
5801         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5802             ok = false;
5803         if (!ok)
5804             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5805         return rtype;
5806     }
5807 
5808     /**
5809      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5810      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5811      *
5812      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5813      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5814      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5815      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5816      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5817      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5818      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5819      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5820      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5821      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5822      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5823      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5824      */
5825     /*non-public*/
5826     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5827         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5828     }
5829 
5830     /**
5831      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5832      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5833      *
5834      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5835      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5836      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5837      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5838      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5839      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5840      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5841      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5842      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5843      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5844      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5845      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5846      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5847      */
5848     /*non-public*/
5849     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5850         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5851     }
5852 
5853     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5854         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5855         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5856         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5857         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5858 
5859         MethodType newType = targetType;
5860         LambdaForm lform;
5861         if (filter) {
5862             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5863         } else {
5864             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5865             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5866             if (!dropResult) {
5867                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5868             }
5869         }
5870         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5871         return result;
5872     }
5873 
5874     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5875         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5876         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5877             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5878         }
5879         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5880 
5881         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5882             int arg = argPos[i];
5883             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5884                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5885             }
5886             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5887                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5888                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5889                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5890             }
5891         }
5892         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5893             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5894         }
5895         return rtype;
5896     }
5897 
5898     /**
5899      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5900      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5901      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5902      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5903      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5904      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5905      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5906      * <p>
5907      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5908      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5909      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5910      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5911      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5912      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5913      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5914      * boolean test(A...);
5915      * T target(A...,B...);
5916      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5917      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5918      *   if (test(a...))
5919      *     return target(a..., b...);
5920      *   else
5921      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5922      * }
5923      * }</pre></blockquote>
5924      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5925      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5926      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5927      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5928      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5929      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5930      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5931      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5932      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5933      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5934      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5935      */
5936     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5937                                MethodHandle target,
5938                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5939         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5940         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5941         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5942         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
