5943             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5944         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5945             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5946         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5947         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5948         if (test == null) {
5949             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5950         }
5951         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5952     }
5953 
5954     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5955         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5956     }
5957 
5958     /**
5959      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5960      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5961      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5962      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5963      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5964      * <p>
5965      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5966      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5967      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5968      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5969      * <p>
5970      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5971      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5972      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5973      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5974      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5975      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5976      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5977      * T target(A..., B...);
5978      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5979      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5980      *   try {
5981      *     return target(a..., b...);
5982      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5983      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5984      *   }
5985      * }
5986      * }</pre></blockquote>
5987      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5988      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5989      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5990      * <p>
5991      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5992      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5993      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5994      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5995      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5996      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5997      * @param target method handle to call
5998      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5999      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
6000      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
6001      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
6002      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
6003      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
6004      *          not match in their return types and their
6005      *          corresponding parameters
6006      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6007      */
6008     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
6009                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
6010                                 MethodHandle handler) {
6011         MethodType ttype = target.type();
6012         MethodType htype = handler.type();
6013         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6014             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6015         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
6016             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
6017             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
6018         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
6019             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
6020         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
6021         if (handler == null) {
6022             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
6023         }
6024         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
6025     }
6026 
6027     /**
6028      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
6029      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
6030      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
6031      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
6032      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
6033      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
6034      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
6035      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
6036      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
6037      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
6038      */
6039     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
6040         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
6041             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
6042         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
6043     }
6044 
6045     /**
6046      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
6047      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
6048      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
6049      * <p>
6050      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
6051      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
6052      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
6053      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
6054      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
6055      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
6056      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
6057      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
6058      * </ul>
6059      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
6060      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
6061      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
6062      * <p>
6063      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
6064      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
6065      * <p>
6066      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
6067      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
6068      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
6069      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
6070      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
6071      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
6072      * <p>
6073      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
6074      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
6075      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
6076      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
6077      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
6078      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
6079      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
6080      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
6081      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
6082      * <p>
6083      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
6084      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
6085      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
6086      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
6087      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
6088      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
6089      * <a id="astar"></a>
6090      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
6091      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
6092      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
6093      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
6094      * <p>
6095      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
6096      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
6097      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
6098      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
6099      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
6100      * <p>
6101      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
6102      * <a id="effid"></a>
6103      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
6104      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
6105      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
6106      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
6107      * that longest list.
6108      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
6109      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
6110      * <p>
6111      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
6112      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
6113      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
6114      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
6115      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
6116      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
6117      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
6118      * </ol>
6119      * <p>
6120      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
6121      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
6122      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
6123      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
6124      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
6125      * iteration variable type.
6126      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
6127      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
6128      * </ol>
6129      * <p>
6130      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
6131      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
6132      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
6133      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
6134      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
6135      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
6136      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
6137      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
6138      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
6139      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
6140      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
6141      * the "internal parameter list".
6142      * </ul>
6143      * <p>
6144      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
6145      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
6146      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
6147      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
6148      * type.
6149      * </ol>
6150      * <p>
6151      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
6152      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
6153      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
6154      * </ol>
6155      * <p>
6156      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
6157      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6158      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
6159      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
6160      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
6161      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
6162      * </ol>
6163      * <p>
6164      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
6165      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
6166      * type.
6167      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
6168      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
6169      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
6170      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
6171      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
6172      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
6173      * loop return type.
6174      * </ol>
6175      * <p>
6176      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
6177      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
6178      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
6179      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
6180      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
6181      * pad out the end of the list.
6182      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
6183      * </ol>
6184      * <p>
6185      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
6186      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
6187      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6188      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6189      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
6190      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
6191      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
6192      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
6193      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
6194      * </ol>
6195      * <p>
6196      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
6197      * <ul>
6198      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
6199      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
6200      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
6201      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
6202      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
6203      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
6204      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
6205      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
6206      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
6207      * </ul>
6208      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
6209      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
6210      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
6211      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
6212      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
6213      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
6214      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
6215      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
6216      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
6217      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
6218      * <p>
6219      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
6220      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
6221      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
6222      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
6223      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
6224      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
6225      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
6226      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
6227      * (in argument order).
6228      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
6229      * returns {@code false}.
6230      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
6231      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
6232      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
6233      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
6234      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
6235      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
6236      * except by throwing an exception.
6237      * </ol>
6238      * <p>
6239      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
6240      * <ul>
6241      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
6242      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
6243      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
6244      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
6245      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
6246      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
6247      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
6248      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
6249      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
6250      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
6251      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
6252      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
6253      * </ul>
6254      * <p>
6255      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
6256      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
6257      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
6258      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6259      * V... init...(A...);
6260      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
6261      * V... step...(V..., A...);
6262      * R fini...(V..., A...);
6263      * R loop(A... a) {
6264      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
6265      *   for (;;) {
6266      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
6267      *       v = s(v..., a...);
6268      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
6269      *         return f(v..., a...);
6270      *       }
6271      *     }
6272      *   }
6273      * }
6274      * }</pre></blockquote>
6275      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
6276      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
6277      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
6278      *
6279      * @apiNote Example:
6280      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6281      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6282      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
6283      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
6284      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
6285      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
6286      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
6287      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6288      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6289      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6290      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6291      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6292      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
6293      * }</pre></blockquote>
6294      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
6295      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6296      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6297      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
6298      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
6299      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
6300      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
6301      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6302      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6303      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
6304      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6305      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6306      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6307      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6308      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6309      * }</pre></blockquote>
6310      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6311      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6312      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6313      * static class FacLoop {
6314      *   final int k;
6315      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6316      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6317      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6318      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6319      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6320      * }
6321      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6322      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6323      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6324      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6325      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6326      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6327      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6328      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6329      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6330      * }</pre></blockquote>
6331      *
6332      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6333      *
6334      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6335      *
6336      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6337      *
6338      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6339      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6340      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6341      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6342      * @since 9
6343      */
6344     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6345         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6346         loopChecks0(clauses);
6347 
6348         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6349         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6350         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6351         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6352 
6353         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6354             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6355             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6356             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6357             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6358         });
6359 
6360         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6361         final int nclauses = init.size();
6362 
6363         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6364         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6365         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6366             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6367             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6368             if (in == null && st == null) {
6369                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6370             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6371                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6372                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6373             } else {
6374                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6375             }
6376         }
6377         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6378                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6379 
6380         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6381         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6382         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6383 
6384         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6385         // Step 1D: check other types.
6386         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6387         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6388                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6389         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6390         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6391 
6392         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6393         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6394         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6395         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6396 
6397         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6398         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6399             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6400             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6401                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6402             }
6403             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6404                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6405             }
6406             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6407                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6408             }
6409             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6410                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6411             }
6412         }
6413 
6414         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6415         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6416         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6417         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6418         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6419         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6420 
6421         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6422                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6423         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6424                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6425 
6426         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6427     }
6428 
6429     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6430         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6431             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6432         }
6433         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6434             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6435         }
6436         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6437             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6438         }
6439     }
6440 
6441     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6442         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6443             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6444                     st.type().returnType());
6445         }
6446     }
6447 
6448     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6449         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6450         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6451                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6452                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6453                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6454                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6455                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6456         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6457     }
6458 
6459     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6460         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6461         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6462     }
6463 
6464     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6465         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6466         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6467         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6468     }
6469 
6470     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6471         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6472                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6473             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6474                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6475         }
6476     }
6477 
6478     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6479         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6480                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6481             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6482                     loopReturnType + ")");
6483         }
6484 
6485         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6486             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6487         }
6488         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6489                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6490             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6491         }
6492     }
6493 
6494     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6495         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6496                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6497             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6498                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6499         }
6500     }
6501 
6502     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6503         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6504             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6505             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6506             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6507         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6508     }
6509 
6510     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6511         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6512     }
6513 
6514     /**
6515      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6516      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6517      * <p>
6518      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6519      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6520      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6521      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6522      * <p>
6523      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6524      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6525      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6526      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6527      * <p>
6528      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6529      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6530      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6531      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6532      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6533      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6534      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6535      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6536      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6537      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6538      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6539      * additional state variable of the loop.
6540      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6541      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6542      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6543      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6544      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6545      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6546      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6547      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6548      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6549      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6550      * </ul>
6551      * <p>
6552      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6553      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6554      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6555      * from the external parameter list.
6556      * </ul>
6557      * <p>
6558      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6559      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6560      * passed to the loop.
6561      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6562      * V init(A...);
6563      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6564      * V body(V, A...);
6565      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6566      *   V v = init(a...);
6567      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6568      *     v = body(v, a...);
6569      *   }
6570      *   return v;
6571      * }
6572      * }</pre></blockquote>
6573      *
6574      * @apiNote Example:
6575      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6576      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6577      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6578      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6579      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6580      *   zip.add(a.next());
6581      *   zip.add(b.next());
6582      *   return zip;
6583      * }
6584      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6585      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6586      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6587      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6588      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6589      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6590      * }</pre></blockquote>
6591      *
6592      *
6593      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6594      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6595      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6596      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6597      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6598      *     MethodHandle[]
6599      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6600      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6601      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6602      * }
6603      * }</pre></blockquote>
6604      *
6605      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6606      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6607      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6608      *             above for other constraints.
6609      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6610      *             See above for other constraints.
6611      *
6612      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6613      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6614      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6615      *
6616      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6617      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6618      * @since 9
6619      */
6620     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6621         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6622         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6623         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6624         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6625         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6626     }
6627 
6628     /**
6629      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6630      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6631      * <p>
6632      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6633      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6634      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6635      * <p>
6636      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6637      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6638      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6639      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6640      * <p>
6641      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6642      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6643      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6644      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6645      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6646      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6647      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6648      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6649      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6650      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6651      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6652      * additional state variable of the loop.
6653      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6654      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6655      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6656      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6657      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6658      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6659      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6660      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6661      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6662      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6663      * </ul>
6664      * <p>
6665      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6666      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6667      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6668      * from the external parameter list.
6669      * </ul>
6670      * <p>
6671      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6672      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6673      * passed to the loop.
6674      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6675      * V init(A...);
6676      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6677      * V body(V, A...);
6678      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6679      *   V v = init(a...);
6680      *   do {
6681      *     v = body(v, a...);
6682      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6683      *   return v;
6684      * }
6685      * }</pre></blockquote>
6686      *
6687      * @apiNote Example:
6688      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6689      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6690      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6691      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6692      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6693      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6694      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6695      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6696      * }</pre></blockquote>
6697      *
6698      *
6699      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6700      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6701      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6702      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6703      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6704      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6705      *     return loop(clause);
6706      * }
6707      * }</pre></blockquote>
6708      *
6709      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6710      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6711      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6712      *             See above for other constraints.
6713      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6714      *             above for other constraints.
6715      *
6716      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6717      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6718      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6719      *
6720      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6721      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6722      * @since 9
6723      */
6724     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6725         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6726         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6727         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6728         return loop(clause);
6729     }
6730 
6731     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6732         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6733         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6734         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6735         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6736         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6737         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6738         if (returnType == void.class) {
6739             // OK
6740         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6741             // leading V argument missing => error
6742             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6743             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6744         } else {
6745             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6746         }
6747         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6748         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6749                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6750             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6751         }
6752         if (init != null) {
6753             MethodType initType = init.type();
6754             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6755                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6756                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6757             }
6758         }
6759     }
6760 
6761     /**
6762      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6763      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6764      * <p>
6765      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6766      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6767      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6768      * <p>
6769      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6770      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6771      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6772      * <p>
6773      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6774      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6775      * iteration variable.
6776      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6777      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6778      * <p>
6779      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6780      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6781      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6782      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6783      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6784      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6785      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6786      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6787      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6788      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6789      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6790      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6791      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6792      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6793      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6794      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6795      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6796      * additional state variable of the loop.
6797      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6798      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6799      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6800      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6801      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6802      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6803      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6804      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6805      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6806      * </ul>
6807      * <p>
6808      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6809      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6810      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6811      * from the external parameter list.
6812      * </ul>
6813      * <p>
6814      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6815      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6816      * arguments passed to the loop.
6817      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6818      * int iterations(A...);
6819      * V init(A...);
6820      * V body(V, int, A...);
6821      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6822      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6823      *   V v = init(a...);
6824      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6825      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6826      *   }
6827      *   return v;
6828      * }
6829      * }</pre></blockquote>
6830      *
6831      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6832      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6833      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6834      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6835      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6836      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6837      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6838      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6839      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6840      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6841      * }</pre></blockquote>
6842      *
6843      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6844      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6845      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6846      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6847      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6848      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6849      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6850      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6851      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6852      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6853      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6854      * }</pre></blockquote>
6855      *
6856      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6857      * as loop parameters:
6858      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6859      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6860      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6861      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6862      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6863      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6864      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6865      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6866      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6867      * }</pre></blockquote>
6868      *
6869      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6870      * to enforce a loop type:
6871      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6872      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6873      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6874      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6875      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6876      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6877      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6878      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6879      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6880      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6881      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6882      * }</pre></blockquote>
6883      *
6884      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6885      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6886      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6887      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6888      * }
6889      * }</pre></blockquote>
6890      *
6891      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6892      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6893      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6894      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6895      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6896      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6897      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6898      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6899      *             See above for other constraints.
6900      *
6901      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6902      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6903      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6904      *
6905      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6906      * @since 9
6907      */
6908     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6909         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6910     }
6911 
6912     /**
6913      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6914      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6915      * <p>
6916      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6917      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6918      * values of the loop counter.
6919      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6920      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6921      * <p>
6922      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6923      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6924      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6925      * <p>
6926      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6927      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6928      * iteration variable.
6929      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6930      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6931      * <p>
6932      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6933      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6934      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6935      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6936      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6937      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6938      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6939      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6940      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6941      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6942      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6943      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6944      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6945      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6946      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6947      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6948      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6949      * additional state variable of the loop.
6950      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6951      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6952      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6953      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6954      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6955      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6956      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6957      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6958      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6959      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6960      * to the external parameter list.
6961      * </ul>
6962      * <p>
6963      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6964      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6965      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6966      * from the external parameter list.
6967      * </ul>
6968      * <p>
6969      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6970      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6971      * arguments passed to the loop.
6972      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6973      * int start(A...);
6974      * int end(A...);
6975      * V init(A...);
6976      * V body(V, int, A...);
6977      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6978      *   int e = end(a...);
6979      *   int s = start(a...);
6980      *   V v = init(a...);
6981      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6982      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6983      *   }
6984      *   return v;
6985      * }
6986      * }</pre></blockquote>
6987      *
6988      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6989      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6990      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6991      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6992      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6993      *     // the following semantics:
6994      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6995      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6996      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6997      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6998      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6999      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
7000      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7001      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7002      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
7003      *     }
7004      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7005      *     MethodHandle[]
7006      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7007      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7008      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7009      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7010      * }
7011      * }</pre></blockquote>
7012      *
7013      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
7014      *              See above for other constraints.
7015      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
7016      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
7017      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7018      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7019      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7020      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7021      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
7022      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7023      *             See above for other constraints.
7024      *
7025      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
7026      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
7027      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
7028      *
7029      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
7030      * @since 9
7031      */
7032     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7033         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
7034         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
7035         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
7036         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
7037         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
7038         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
7039         MethodHandle retv = null;
7040         if (returnType != void.class) {
7041             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
7042             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
7043             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
7044         }
7045         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
7046         MethodHandle[]
7047             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
7048             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
7049             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
7050         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
7051     }
7052 
7053     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7054         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
7055         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
7056         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7057         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
7058         if (counterType != int.class) {
7059             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
7060             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
7061         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
7062             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
7063             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
7064         }
7065         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7066         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7067         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
7068         // strip leading V value if present
7069         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7070         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7071             // argument list has no "V" => error
7072             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7073             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7074         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
7075             // missing I type => error
7076             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
7077             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7078         }
7079         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
7080         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
7081             // special case; take lists from end handle
7082             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
7083             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
7084         }
7085         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
7086         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7087             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
7088         }
7089         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
7090             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7091             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
7092         }
7093         if (init != null) {
7094             MethodType initType = init.type();
7095             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7096                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
7097                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
7098             }
7099         }
7100     }
7101 
7102     /**
7103      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
7104      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
7105      * <p>
7106      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
7107      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
7108      * <p>
7109      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
7110      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
7111      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
7112      * <p>
7113      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
7114      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
7115      * iteration variable.
7116      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
7117      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
7118      * <p>
7119      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
7120      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
7121      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
7122      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
7123      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
7124      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
7125      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
7126      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
7127      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
7128      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
7129      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
7130      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
7131      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
7132      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
7133      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
7134      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
7135      * additional state variable of the loop.
