7136      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
7137      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
7138      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
7139      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
7140      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7141      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
7142      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
7143      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
7144      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
7145      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
7146      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
7147      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
7148      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7149      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
7150      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
7151      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
7152      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
7153      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7154      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
7155      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
7156      * </ul>
7157      * <p>
7158      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
7159      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
7160      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
7161      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7162      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
7163      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
7164      * <p>
7165      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7166      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7167      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7168      * from the external parameter list.
7169      * </ul>
7170      * <p>
7171      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7172      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
7173      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
7174      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7175      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
7176      * V init(A...);
7177      * V body(V,T,A...);
7178      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
7179      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
7180      *   V v = init(a...);
7181      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
7182      *     T t = it.next();
7183      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
7184      *   }
7185      *   return v;
7186      * }
7187      * }</pre></blockquote>
7188      *
7189      * @apiNote Example:
7190      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7191      * // get an iterator from a list
7192      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
7193      *   r.add(0, e);
7194      *   return r;
7195      * }
7196      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
7197      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
7198      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
7199      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
7200      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
7201      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7202      * }</pre></blockquote>
7203      *
7204      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7205      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7206      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7207      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7208      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7209      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7210      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7211      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7212      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7213      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7214      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7215      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7216      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7217      *     }
7218      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7219      *     MethodHandle[]
7220      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7221      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7222      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7223      * }
7224      * }</pre></blockquote>
7225      *
7226      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7227      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7228      *                 See above for other constraints.
7229      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7230      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7231      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7232      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7233      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7234      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7235      *             See above for other constraints.
7236      *
7237      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7238      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7239      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7240      *
7241      * @since 9
7242      */
7243     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7244         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7245         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7246         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7247         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7248         MethodHandle startIter;
7249         MethodHandle nextVal;
7250         {
7251             MethodType iteratorType;
7252             if (iterator == null) {
7253                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
7254                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7255                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7256             } else {
7257                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7258                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7259                 startIter = iterator;
7260             }
7261             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7262             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
7263 
7264             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
7265             try {
7266                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
7267                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
7268             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
7269                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
7270             }
7271         }
7272 
7273         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
7274         if (returnType != void.class) {
7275             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7276             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7277             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7278             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7279         }
7280 
7281         MethodHandle[]
7282             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
7283             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
7284         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7285     }
7286 
7287     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7288         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7289         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7290         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7291         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
7292         // strip leading V value if present
7293         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7294         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7295             // argument list has no "V" => error
7296             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7297             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7298         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
7299             // missing T type => error
7300             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
7301             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7302         }
7303         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
7304         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7305         if (iterator != null) {
7306             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7307             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7308             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7309                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7310             }
7311             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7312             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7313                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7314             }
7315             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7316                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7317                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7318             }
7319         } else {
7320             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7321                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7322                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7323                 // of Iterable
7324                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7325                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7326             } else {
7327                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7328                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7329                 // assignable to Iterable
7330                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7331                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7332                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7333                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7334                 }
7335             }
7336         }
7337         if (init != null) {
7338             MethodType initType = init.type();
7339             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7340                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7341                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7342             }
7343         }
7344         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7345     }
7346 
7347     /*non-public*/
7348     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7349         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7350         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7351         int[] order = new int[arity];
7352         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7353         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7354         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7355         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7356         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7357         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7358     }
7359 
7360     /**
7361      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7362      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7363      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7364      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7365      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7366      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7367      * <p>
7368      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7369      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7370      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7371      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7372      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7373      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7374      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7375      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7376      * <p>
7377      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7378      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7379      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7380      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7381      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7382      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7383      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7384      * </ul>
7385      * <p>
7386      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7387      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7388      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7389      * the cleanup.
7390      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7391      * V target(A..., B...);
7392      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7393      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7394      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7395      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7396      *   try {
7397      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7398      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7399      *     throwable = t;
7400      *     throw t;
7401      *   } finally {
7402      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7403      *   }
7404      *   return result;
7405      * }
7406      * }</pre></blockquote>
7407      * <p>
7408      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7409      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7410      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7411      * <p>
7412      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7413      * always throws.
7414      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7415      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7416      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7417      * <p>
7418      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7419      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7420      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7421      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7422      * <p>
7423      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
7424      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
7425      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
7426      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
7427      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
7428      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
7429      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
7430      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
7431      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
7432      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
7433      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
7434      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
7435      *
7436      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
7437      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
7438      *
7439      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
7440      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
7441      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
7442      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
7443      *          not match in their return types and their
7444      *          corresponding trailing parameters
7445      *
7446      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
7447      * @since 9
7448      */
7449     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7450         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
7451         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7452 
7453         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
7454 
7455         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
7456         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7457         // target parameter list.
7458         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
7459 
7460         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
7461         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
7462         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
7463 
7464         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
7465         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
7466     }
7467 
7468     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7469         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7470         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
7471             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
7472         }
7473         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
7474         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
7475             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
7476         }
7477         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
7478             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
7479         }
7480         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7481         // target parameter list.
7482         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
7483         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
7484             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
7485                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
7486         }
7487     }
7488 
7489 }
